<Rate>3< /Rate>< Review>
Found this small place by off chance.

They make their own ice cream and even have a vegan option as well.

The grill area is small and all the food is made to order. Their menu is small and it covers just about everything you may want to eat, as long as it comes on bread, wrapped, or a salad.

Today they were out of (3) ice cream flavors, which seems odd. If they make their own on site, why not do so on a daily basis, or if one sells out?

The service was as good as to be expected.

We only have one scoop each; Strawberry (tasted like strawberry quick) and Swiss Chip Orange (tasted like a chocolate orange; you know the one that is sold around the holiday?)< /Review>

<Rate>5< /Rate><Text>Absolutely, one of the best homemade
ice-creams & Banana Splits anywhere in our
country!  I should know, since I was an Carvel
Ice-cream store manager when I was a teen in
NYC.
Tons of flavor choices, that taste amazing!
Most choices are not made overly sweet,
but just right.
It is a hidden humble place, well known by locals
over decades.  They almost went out of business
a few years back due to an ownership change.
The locals basically "screamed for ice-cream" and
the new owners probably realized that they
had a sure thing going on.
Inside it is not fancy, but is very comfortable, with
comfy old style booths.
Besides or before you get the "required" Sundae
or BS, they do have a nice selection of dinner type
eats.  They are all quite good & made fresh.
Their service comes with lots of smiles & they are
more than happy to have you try lots of samples
as you decide what scoops to place on your BS.
Their BS is no BS!
This old school Ice-cream shop is one of few
gems in otherwise boring Modesto.  Thanks!</Text><pictures>None<//pictures>< Resp>

<user_name>Corsentino</user_name><date>1565365547374< /date><Rate>4<//Rate>< review>
I've been working in this area for 3 years. I would've never stepped into this place had it not been recommended by a Vietnamese co-worker. It just didn't look like what I expected at all from the outside. All these years i'd assumed it was a classic sports bar. But that was far from reality. Inside yes, there's a bar, but the menu is clearly Viet - without question. A quick overview of the clientele confirms this. And its pretty good too. I recommend the bun bo Hue, and would come back. My only knock on this place is that it is not obvious from the outside. I would never have even considered it and would've gone on thinking it was an American sports bar forever had I not been informed otherwise.

So here I am to inform you, good reader, that it is a Viet restaurant, not a sports bar.</review>

<text>A really interesting place.  Wholly Vietnamese owned and run but feels almost like a night club vs. a traditional Vietnamese eatery.  It is very modern in design and decor but the food is pretty legit. Even the crowd is a mix of young and trendy folk mixed with business lunch crowds and traditional patronage of the older generation.  The Bo Luc Lac (sp?) is just like mom's and very tasty and the Bun Bo Hue I had was flavorful (though on the lighter side relative to other establishments) and my companion really enjoyed his Pho.  In addition, the bar attendant knew all the beers on tap but with a mid/heavy Vietnamese accent.  Not something I am used to hearing and really impressed.  I recommend this place for authentic Viet food in a non traditional modern environment and look forward to trying other dishes here in the future.<//text><Gmap_id>0x808fcc0ec732076d:0x70de2f9b4e845412</Gmap_id>< Rate>

Anthony Lee< /username>
< Text>
As we arrived to the restaurant, the entrance was a bit odd because you had to go right into the patio to get to the front door. The restaurant was pretty busy but we were able to get a seat relatively quick.
As we looked through the menu, we noticed the food was a bit pricey, but decided to stay because we came here for the fried calamari. We ended up ordering the fried calamari and seafood chow mein. The fried calamari came out first and it was pretty tasty. It came with a side of sweet chili sauce. The chow mein seemed to take much longer to make. In between, they brought out the wrong order which was some chicken wings. I let them know right away we didn't order any wings.
Overall, the fried calamari was pretty tasty, but the seafood chow mein was nothing special. Both dishes were $18 each so there wasn't much value. After tax and tip, it was $40 ish for an appetizer and noodles.
We don't plan to come back which is too bad because the fried calamari was good. Another down side was there wasn't much service after we got our food.<//Text>

The Lunch Buffet dessert has Rosmalai! New restaurant, so as expected -decor is shiny clean and food presentations sharp. Waiters were attentive, food is fresh. Review after two visits.
Lunch Buffet: good selection. "Shaag" was good. Kebab items make the mark. A little too much salt (cliche in many Indian Buffets).

Tried a dinner a la carte. Got a platter with Chicken, lamb and lamb rack + shrimp. Can be shared by two. Get an extra naan. The included naan is only two pieces, not two whole naan. I was unpressed by the rack of lamb and shrimp.</Review>

< text>
Ever since Sneha changed ownership and name to Marigold, the quality went down, and they cut out most of the dishes that I liked. Since then, I've been looking for a replacement Indian lunch buffet, and Sakoon is it for right now.

They can be very busy during the week at lunch. The first time I went, I left because the buffet line was wrapping back into the room at the back of the restaurant.

Their goat curry is very good. Lots of flavor, a little heat, and the goat is very tender.

None of the dishes I had disappointed me.

They also have a nice vegetarian selection. The lunch buffet is about $15.<//text>

< text>
Took 14 people from work to this place today . We were all there for the first time . Loved the food , good quality , not too spicy or greasy . Just perfect

The only reason why it's a 3 star and not a five star is coz the actual food during the buffet is tucked inside a corner and the lines run very very very long ( about 35+people) . . had to wait 23 minutes in the food line to get my first plate and then didn't want to get back in the line . Wish they had a center table or laid it out somewhere outside so it's better approachable and the line moves faster . This was a horrendous wait for a single plate during buffet .
